## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa

70-assistanttext-
The migration guide has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what was documented:

---

## What Was Found and Documented

### Breaking Changes
- **Mutual exclusion of `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`**: In v1.31, setting both fields with non-default values causes Envoy to throw an exception at startup and refuse to start. This is enforced in `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` in the `FilterConfig` constructor.

### Deprecated Features
- **`disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11)**: Marked for future removal via `udpa.annotations.field_migrate` (oneof promotion), added to `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`. The field is silently mapped to `RouteCacheAction::RETAIN` internally. Operators should migrate to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.

### New Features
1. **`RouteCacheAction` enum + `route_cache_action` field (field 18)**: Three-way route cache control (`DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, `RETAIN`) replacing the binary `disable_clear_route_cache` flag.

2. **`deferred_close_timeout` field (field 19)**: A `google.protobuf.Duration` field (default 5s) that caps how long Envoy holds open a gRPC stream to the external processor in `observability_mode`. Backed by the new `ThreadLocalStreamManager` / `DeferredDeletableStream` infrastructure in `ext_proc.h`.

3. **`observability_mode` hardening**: The `Filter::encodeComplete()` override now triggers `logGrpcStreamInfo()`, and outbound `ProcessingRequest` messages now carry `observability_mode: true` so external processors know not to send responses.

    "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n15: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n16: \n17: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n18: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\n20: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n22: \n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n24: // External Processing Filter\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n26: \n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n28: \n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n31: //\n32: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n33: \n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n36: //\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n41: //\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n44: // and how it should be processed.\n45: //\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n47: //\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n53: //\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\n57: //\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n63: //   to SEND.\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n118: \n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n122: \n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n129: \n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n136: \n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n147:     gte {}\n148:   }];\n149: \n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\n153: \n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n156:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n159:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n166: \n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n172:     gte {}\n173:   }];\n174: \n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n179: \n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n183: \n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n188: \n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n195: \n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n202: \n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n205: \n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n209:   //\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n212:   //\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n214:   // This also means that\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n217:   //\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n219:   //\n220:   // .. warning::\n221:   //\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n227:   //\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\n229: }\n230: \n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n232: // dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n233: // metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\n234: message MetadataOptions {\n235:   message MetadataNamespaces {\n236:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n237:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n238:     repeated string untyped = 1;\n239: \n240:     // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n241:     // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n242:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n243:     // definition for safe parsing.\n244:     repeated string typed = 2;\n245:   }\n246: \n247:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n248:   // the external processing server.\n249:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n250: \n251:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n252:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n255: }\n256: \n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n259: //\n260: // This works as below:\n261: //\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n265: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n266: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n267: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n268: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n269: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n270:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n271:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n272:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n273: \n274:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n275:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n276:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n277: }\n278: \n279: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n280: // virtual host or cluster.\n281: message ExtProcPerRoute {\n282:   oneof override {\n283:     option (validate.required) = true;\n284: \n285:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n286:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n287:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n288: \n289:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n290:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n291:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\n292:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n293:   }\n294: }\n295: \n296: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n297: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n298: message ExtProcOverrides {\n299:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n300:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n301: \n302:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n303:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n304:   bool async_mode = 2;\n305: \n306:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n307:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n308:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\n309:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n310: \n311:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n312:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n313:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\n314:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n315: \n316:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n317:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n318: \n319:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n320:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n321:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n322:   // config used. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n138: \\n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n140:   // sent. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. This allows to distinguish\\n171:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\\n172:   string stat_prefix = 8;\\n173: \\n174:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\\n175:   // make to message headers. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n234:   //\\n235:   // .. warning::\\n236:   //\\n237:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n238:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n239:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n240:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n241:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n242:   //\\n243:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n244: \\n245:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n246:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n247:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n248:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\\n249:   // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\\n250:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\\n251:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \\\"clear_route_cache_type\\\"];\\n252: \\n253:   // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\\n254:   // received in response to request headers. [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. If not\n164:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n165:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n166:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n167:     gte {}\n168:   }];\n169: \n170:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n27:     // while trailers are skipped.\n28:     DEFAULT = 0;\n29: \n30:     // Send the header or trailer.\n31:     SEND = 1;\n32: \n33:     // Do not send the header or trailer.\n34:     SKIP = 2;\n35:   }\n36: \n37:   // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n38:   // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n39:   // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n40:   // to be set correctly:\n41:   // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n42:   // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n43:   // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n44:   //\n45:   // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n46:   // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\n47:   // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\n48:   // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\n49:   //\n50:   // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\n51:   // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\n52:   // of mutated body. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\n53:   // local reply will be sent with an error message.\n54:   enum BodySendMode {\n55:     // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\n56:     NONE = 0;\n57: \n58:     // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n59:     // proxy.\n60:     STREAMED = 1;\n61: \n62:     // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n63:     // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n64:     // downstream system will receive an error.\n65:     BUFFERED = 2;\n66: \n67:     // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n68:     // chunk. If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the body contents\n69:     // up to the buffer limit will be sent.\n70:     BUFFERED_PARTIAL = 3;\n71:   }\n72: \n73:   // How to handle the request header. Default is \"SEND\".\n74:   HeaderSendMode request_header_mode = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n75: \n76:   // How to handle the response header. Default is \"NONE\".\n80:   BodySendMode request_body_mode = 3 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n81: \n82:   // How do handle the response body. Default is \"NONE\".\n83:   BodySendMode response_body_mode = 4 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n84: \n85:   // How to handle the request trailers. state, Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\\n388:   if (end_stream) {\\n389:     state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\\n390:   }\\n391:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\\n392:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\\\");\\n393:     data.drain(data.length());\\n394:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n395:   }\\n396:   if (processing_complete_) {\\n397:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Continuing (processing complete)\\\");\\n398:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n399:   }\\n400: \\n401:   if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\\n402:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\\\");\\n403:     // We don't know what to do with the body    // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\\n407:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\\n408:     // buffer limit.\\n409:     state.setPaused(true);\\n410:     state.requestWatermark();\\n411:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\\n412:   }\\n413: \\n414:   FilterDataStatus mode works as follows:\\n445:     //\\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \\\"moves\\\" the data into a new buffer, which it\\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n449:     // out of memory.\\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n452:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n454:     // injected.)\\n455:     //\\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n466:       // Fall through\\n467:       break;\\n468:     }\\n469: \\n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n474: \\n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n476:     if (end_stream) {\\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n480:     } else {\\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n482:     }\\n483:     break;\\n484:   }\\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n487:     //\\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\\n490:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\\n491:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\\n492:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\\n493:     // buffered mode.\\n494:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\\n495:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\\n496:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\\n497:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\\n498:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\\n499:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\\n500:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\\n501:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Partial buffer limit reached\\\");\\n502:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\\n503:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\\n504:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\\n505:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n506:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\\n507:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\\n508:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\\n509:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\\n510:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n511:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Call in progress for partial mode\\\");\\n512:       state.setPaused(true);\\n513:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n514:     } else {\\n515:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n516:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\\n517:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\\n518:         // to the processor.\\n519:         bool terminate;\\n520:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\\n521:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\\n522:         if (terminate) {\\n523:           return chunk_result;\\n524:         }\\n525:       }\\n526:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n527:     }\\n528:     break;\\n529:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n530:   default:\\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n532:     break;\\n533:   }\\n534: \\n535:   return result;\\n536: }\\n537: \\n538: std::pair<bool, state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n390:   }\n391:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\n392:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\");\n393:     data.drain(data.length());\n394:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n395:   }\n396:   if (processing_complete_) {\n397:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Continuing (processing complete)\");\n398:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n399:   }\n400: \n401:   if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\n402:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\");\n403:     // We don't know what to do with the body until the response comes back.\n404:     // We must buffer it in case we need it when that happens.\n405:     // Raise a watermark to prevent a buffer overflow until the response comes back.\n406:     // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\n407:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\n408:     // buffer limit.\n409:     state.setPaused(true);\n410:     state.requestWatermark();\n411:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n412:   }\n413: \n414:   FilterDataStatus result;\n415:   switch (state.bodyMode()) {\n416:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED:\n417:     if (end_stream) {\n418:       switch (openStream()) {\n419:       case StreamOpenState::Error:\n420:         return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n421:       case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n422: to send the buffer\n429:       ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending request body message\");\n430:       state.addBufferedData(data);\n431:       auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), end_stream);\n432:       sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n433:       // Since we just just moved the data into the buffer, return NoBuffer\n434:       // so that we do not buffer this chunk twice.\n435:       state.setPaused(true);\n436:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n437:       break;\n438:     }\n439:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onData: Buffering\");\n440:     state.setPaused(true);\n441:     result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndBuffer;\n442:     break;\n443:   case ProcessingMode::STREAMED: {\n444:     // STREAMED body mode works as follows:\n445:     //\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \"moves\" the data into a new buffer, which it\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\n449:     // out of memory.\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\n452:     // into the filter chain using \"inject**codedData\". (The processor may respond indicating that\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\n454:     // injected.)\n455:     //\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n466:       // Fall through\n467:       break;\n468:     }\n469: \n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\n474: \n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\n476:     if (end_stream) {\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n480:     } else {\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n482:     }\n483:     break;\n484:   }\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\n487:     //\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\n490:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\n491:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\n492:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\n493:     // buffered mode.\n494:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\n495:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\n496:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\n497:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\n498:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\n499:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\n500:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\n501:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Partial buffer limit reached\");\n502:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\n503:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\n504:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\n505:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n506:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\n507:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\n508:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\n509:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\n510:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n511:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Call in progress for partial mode\");\n512:       state.setPaused(true);\n513:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n514:     } else {\n515:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n516:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\n517:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\n518:         // to the processor.\n519:         bool terminate;\n520:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\n521:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\n522:         if (terminate) {\n523:           return chunk_result;\n524:         }\n525:       }\n526:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n527:     }\n528:     break;\n529:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\n530:   default:\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n532:     break;\n533:   }\n534: \n535:   return result;\n536: }\n537: \n538: std::pair<bool, Http::FilterDataStatus> (The processor may respond indicating that\\n542:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n543:     // injected.)\\n544:     //\\n545:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n546:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n547:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n548:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n549:     switch (openStream()) {\\n550:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n551:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n552:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n553:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n554:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n555:       // Fall through\\n556:       break;\\n557:     }\\n558: \\n559:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n560:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n561:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n562:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n563: \\n564:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n565:     if (end_stream) {\\n566:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n567:       state.setPaused(true);\\n568:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n569:     } else {\\n570:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n571:     }\\n572:     break;\\n573:   }\\n574:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n575:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n576:     //\\n577:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n578:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\\n579:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\\n580:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\\n581:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\\n582:     // buffered mode.\\n583:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\\n584:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\\n585:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\\n586:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\\n587:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\\n588:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\\n589:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\\n590:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Partial buffer limit reached\\\");\\n591:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\\n592:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\\n593:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\\n594:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n595:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\\n596:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\\n597:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\\n598:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\\n599:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n600:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Call in progress for partial mode\\\");\\n601:       state.setPaused(true);\\n602:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n603:     } else {\\n604:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n605:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\\n606:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\\n607:         // to the processor.\\n608:         bool terminate;\\n609:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\\n610:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\\n611:         if (terminate) {\\n612:           return chunk_result;\\n613:         }\\n614:       }\\n615:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n616:     }\\n617:     break;\\n618:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n619:   default:\\n620:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n621:     break;\\n622:   }\\n623: \\n624:   return result;\\n625: }\\n626: \\n627: ProcessingRequest Filter::buildHeaderRequest(ProcessorState& state,\\n628:                                              Http::RequestOrResponseHeaderMap& headers,\\n629:                                              bool end_stream, bool observability_mode) {\\n630:   ProcessingRequest req;\\n631:   if (observability_mode) {\\n632:     req.set_observability_mode(true);\\n633:   }\\n634:   addAttributes(state,          Http::RequestOrResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) {\n417:   switch (openStream()) {\n418:   case StreamOpenState::Error:\n419:     return FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration;\n420: sendDataInObservabilityMode(data, state, end_stream);\n475:   }\n476: \n477:   if (end_stream) {\n478:     state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n479:   }\n480:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\n481:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\");\n482:     data.drain(data.length());\n483:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n484:   }\n485:   if (processing_complete_) {\n486:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Continuing (processing complete)\");\n487:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n488:   }\n489: \n490:   if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\n491:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\");\n492:     // We don't know what to do with the body until the response comes back.\n493:     // We must buffer it in case we need it when that happens.\n494:     // Raise a watermark to prevent a buffer overflow until the response comes back.\n495:     // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\n496:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\n497:     // buffer limit.\n498:     state.setPaused(true);\n499:     state.requestWatermark();\n500:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n501:   }\n502: \n503:   FilterDataStatus result;\n504:   switch (state.bodyMode()) {\n505:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED:\n506:     if (end_stream) {\n507:       switch (openStream()) {\n508:       case StreamOpenState::Error:\n509:         return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n510:       case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n511:         return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n512:       case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n513:         // Fall through\n514:         break;\n515:       }\n516: \n517:       // The body has been buffered and we need to send the buffer\n518:       ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending request body message\");\n519:       state.addBufferedData(data);\n520:       auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), end_stream);\n521:       sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n522:       // Since we just just moved the data into the buffer, return NoBuffer\n523:       // so that we do not buffer this chunk twice.\n524:       state.setPaused(true);\n525:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n526:       break;\n527:     }\n528:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onData: Buffering\");\n529:     state.setPaused(true);\n530:     result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndBuffer;\n531:     break;\n532:   case ProcessingMode::STREAMED: {\n533:     // STREAMED body mode works as follows:\n534:     //\n535:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \"moves\" the data into a new buffer, which it\n536:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\n537:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\n538:     // out of memory.\n539:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\n540:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\n541:     // into the filter chain using \"inject**codedData\". (The processor may respond indicating that\n542:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\n543:     // injected.)\n544:     //\n545:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\n546:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\n547:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\n548:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\n549:     switch (openStream()) {\n550:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\n551:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n552:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n553:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n554:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n555:       // Fall through\n556:       break;\n557:     }\n558: \n559:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\n560:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\n561:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n562:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\n563: \n564:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\n565:     if (end_stream) {\n566:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\n567:       state.setPaused(true);\n568:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n569:     } else {\n570:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n571:     }\n572:     break;\n573:   }\n574:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\n575:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\n576:     //\n577:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\n578:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\n579:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\n580:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\n581:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\n582:     // buffered mode.\n583:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\n584:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\n585:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\n586:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\n587:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\n588:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\n589:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\n590:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Partial buffer limit reached\");\n591:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\n592:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\n593:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\n594:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n595:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\n596:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\n597:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\n598:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\n599:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n600:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Call in progress for partial mode\");\n601:       state.setPaused(true);\n602:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n603:     } else {\n604:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n605:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\n606:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\n607:         // to the processor.\n608:         bool terminate;\n609:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\n610:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\n611:         if (terminate) {\n612:           return chunk_result;\n613:         }\n614:       }\n615:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n616:     }\n617:     break;\n618:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\n619:   default:\n620:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n621:     break;\n622:   }\n623: \n624:   return result;\n625: }\n626: \n627: ProcessingRequest Filter::buildHeaderRequest(ProcessorState& state, Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\\n388:   if (end_stream) {\\n389:     state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\\n390:   }\\n391:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\\n392: mode works as follows:\\n445:     //\\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \\\"moves\\\" the data into a new buffer, which it\\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n449:     // out of memory.\\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n452:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n454:     // injected.)\\n455:     //\\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n466:       // Fall through\\n467:       break;\\n468:     }\\n469: \\n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n474: \\n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n476:     if (end_stream) {\\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n480:     } else {\\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n482:     }\\n483:     break;\\n484:   }\\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n487:     //\\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n530:   default:\\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n532:     break;\\n533:   }\\n534: \\n535:   return result;\\n536: }\\n537: \\n538: std::pair<bool, It\\n537:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n538:     // out of memory.\\n539:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n540:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n541:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n542:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n543:     // injected.)\\n544:     //\\n545:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n546:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n547:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n548:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n549:     switch (openStream()) {\\n550:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n551:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n552:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n553:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n554:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n555:       // Fall through\\n556:       break;\\n557:     }\\n558: \\n559:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n560:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n561:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n562:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n563: \\n564:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n565:     if (end_stream) {\\n566:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n567:       state.setPaused(true);\\n568:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n569:     } else {\\n570:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n571:     }\\n572:     break;\\n573:   }\\n574:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n575:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n576:     //\\n577:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n578:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\\n579:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\\n580:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\\n581:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\\n582:     // buffered mode.\\n583:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\\n584:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\\n585:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\\n586:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\\n587:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\\n588:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\\n589:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\\n590:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Partial buffer limit reached\\\");\\n591:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\\n592:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\\n593:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\\n594:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n595:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\\n596:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\\n597:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\\n598:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\\n599:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n600:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Call in end_stream);\\n605:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\\n606:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\\n607:         // to the processor.\\n608:         bool terminate;\\n609:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\\n610:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\\n611:         if (terminate) {\\n612:           return chunk_result;\\n613:         }\\n614:       }\\n615:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n616:     }\\n617:     break;\\n618:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n619:   default:\\n620:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n621:     break;\\n622:   }\\n623: \\n624:   return result;\\n625: }\\n626: \\n627: ProcessingRequest   "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ",
